        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          margin: auto;

          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }

          flex-grow: 0;

        }

          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

<span class="line"><!---->This bug is similiar to <!----></span>





issue 1335861



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1335861" title="Security: heap-use-after-free in SearchNameNodeByNameInternal"><!---->issue 1335861<!----></a>





.



<span class="line"><!---->.<!----></span>



<br>





SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() function could call itself recursively[3] and it calls GetNodeLimitsAndSanitize() to truncate CPDF_Array with length greater then 2 [1][2]. 



<span class="line"><!---->SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() function could call itself recursively[3] and it calls GetNodeLimitsAndSanitize() to truncate CPDF_Array with length greater then 2 [1][2]. <!----></span>





Issue 1335861



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1335861" title="Security: heap-use-after-free in SearchNameNodeByNameInternal"><!---->Issue 1335861<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





have showed it is possible to make dangling pointer.



<span class="line"><!---->have showed it is possible to make dangling pointer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Issue 1335861



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1335861" title="Security: heap-use-after-free in SearchNameNodeByNameInternal"><!---->Issue 1335861<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





has been patched with commit 



<span class="line"><!---->has been patched with commit <!----></span>





3466cc056b052eb5e8e9d7d5f8f2aa3ab33e3bd6



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/3466cc056b052eb5e8e9d7d5f8f2aa3ab33e3bd6"><!---->3466cc056b052eb5e8e9d7d5f8f2aa3ab33e3bd6<!----></a>





 by introducing RetainPtr<> on many places to extend lifetime of accessed CPDF_Object objects. So the CPDF_Object could alive after its owner is removed from GetNodeLimitsAndSanitize().



<span class="line"><!----> by introducing RetainPtr&lt;&gt; on many places to extend lifetime of accessed CPDF_Object objects. So the CPDF_Object could alive after its owner is removed from GetNodeLimitsAndSanitize().<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Unfortunately, this patch is not enough. SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() functions could return dangled CPDF_Object pointer and UAF will occur once accessing returned pointer.



<span class="line"><!---->Unfortunately, this patch is not enough. SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() functions could return dangled CPDF_Object pointer and UAF will occur once accessing returned pointer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() will return pointer once matched object is found in item for "Names" key[4].



<span class="line"><!---->SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() will return pointer once matched object is found in item for "Names" key[4].<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Once matched object isn't found, SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() iterates "Kids" item list[5] and call itself recursively for child [3]. Once some pointer is returned(found), it returns that value[6]. RetainPtr<> is used[7] to prevent "Kids" items being freed during this iteration. Because SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() may free some objects. 



<span class="line"><!---->Once matched object isn't found, SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() iterates "Kids" item list[5] and call itself recursively for child [3]. Once some pointer is returned(found), it returns that value[6]. RetainPtr&lt;&gt; is used[7] to prevent "Kids" items being freed during this iteration. Because SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() may free some objects. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The problem is that RetainPtr<> at [7] prevent object is being freed during iteration only. SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() can returns found object[6] but the lifetime of returned object could be ended within iteration and SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() function scope. As a result, a dangling pointer is returned because the object's lifetime ends at the same time it returns.



<span class="line"><!---->The problem is that RetainPtr&lt;&gt; at [7] prevent object is being freed during iteration only. SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() can returns found object[6] but the lifetime of returned object could be ended within iteration and SearchNameNodeByNameInternal() function scope. As a result, a dangling pointer is returned because the object's lifetime ends at the same time it returns.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>

<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: Stable / 107.0.5269.0 (Commit <!----></span>

)



<span class="line"><!---->)<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Ubuntu 20.04 x64<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->Open `poc.pdf`<!----></span>

<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
